25:T6883,<entryFree id="n30407" key="عَلَى" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">عَلَى</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> is a particle and a noun (Mbr, S, Mughnee, K) and a verb; (Mbr, S;) though some assert that it is only a noun, and ascribe this assertion to Sb: (Mughnee:) its alif, (Sb, S, Msb,) [which, when it has no affix, is written <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>, and] which is originally <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign>, (Sb, S,) [like that of <foreign lang="ar">إِلَى</foreign>, q. v.,] is changed into [what is properly] <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> when it has a pronominal affix, (Sb, S, Msb,) as in <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْكَ</foreign>, (Sb, S,) and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْهِ</foreign>; (Msb;) but some of the Arabs [in this case] leave it unchanged, as in the saying of a rájiz, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">طَارُوا عَلَاهُنَّ فَطِرْ عَلَاهَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">They fled,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">have fled, upon them,</hi> (referring to camels,) <hi rend="ital">and flee thou upon her</hi>]; this, it is said, being of the dial. of Belhárith Ibn-Kaab. (Sb, S.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  As a particle, it has nine [or more than nine] meanings. (Mughnee.) As such, (Mughnee,) or, accord. to Sb, as a noun, (K,) it denotes <foreign lang="ar">الاِسْتِعْلَآء</foreign> [i. e. superiority] (Msb, Es-Subkee, Mughnee, K, TA) properly thus termed, (Msb,) such as is perceptible by sense; (Es-Subkee, TA;) either with respect to what is signified by the noun governed by it, and this is generally the case, (Mughnee,) as in the saying [in the Kur xxiii. 22 and xl. 80], <foreign lang="ar">وَعَلَيْهَا وَعَلَى ٱلْفُلْكِ تُحْمَلُونَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And upon them</hi> (referring to camels) <hi rend="ital">and upon the ship,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ships, ye are carried</hi>]; (Mughnee, K;) or with respect to what is near thereto, as in the saying [in the Kur xx. 10], <foreign lang="ar">أَوْ أَجِدُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى ٱلنَّارِ هُدًى</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Or I shall find near upon the fire,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">at the fire, a right direction</hi>]: (Mughnee:) and using it to denote <foreign lang="ar">الاستعلآء</foreign> properly thus termed, you say, <foreign lang="ar">كُنْتُ عَلَى السَّطْحِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I was</hi> 
                  <pb n="2145"/> 
                  <hi rend="ital">upon the flat house-top</hi>]: (Msb:) [in like manner also,] as denoting <foreign lang="ar">الاستعلآء</foreign> that is perceptible by sense, it occurs in the saying [in the Kur lv. 26], <foreign lang="ar">كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Every one that is upon it</hi> (referring to the earth) <hi rend="ital">is transitory</hi>]: (Es-Subkee, TA:) and you say, <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى زَيْدٍ ثَوْبٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Upon Zeyd is,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">was, a garment</hi>], <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى</foreign> being here a particle; and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَا زَيْدًا ثَوْبٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">A garment was upon Zeyd,</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">عَلَا</foreign> being here a verb. (Mbr, S.) And it denotes <foreign lang="ar">الاستعلآء</foreign>, likewise, tropically thus termed, (Msb, TA,) such as is ideal, or perceived by the intel-lect; (Msb, Es-Subkee, Mughnee, TA;) as in the saying <foreign lang="ar">زَيْدٌ عَلَيْهِ دَيْنٌ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">Zeyd, a debt is lying upon him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">incumbent on him,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">he owes a debt,</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">لِفُلَانٍ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">to such a one</hi>], that which is ideal being thus likened to that which is corporeal; (Msb;) and in the phrases <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْنَا أَمْرٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْنَا مَالٌ</foreign>, meaning <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">An affair,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a command, lies,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">rests, upon us,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">is incumbent on us,</hi> and so <hi rend="ital">property,</hi> [<hi rend="ital">as due from us,</hi> i. e.] <hi rend="ital">the former as a duty</hi> and <hi rend="ital">the latter as a debt,</hi> i. e. <foreign lang="ar">يَثْبُتُ</foreign>, like as the thing lies, or rests, (<foreign lang="ar">يَثْبُتُ</foreign>,) upon the place; the latter phrase importing responsibility: and <foreign lang="ar">ثَبَتَ عَلَيْهِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مَالٌ</foreign> is also said to mean <foreign lang="ar">كَثُرَ</foreign> [i. e. <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">property was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, much in quantity,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">amount, upon him,</hi> app. <hi rend="ital">as a burden imposing upon him responsibility</hi>]. (TA.) And it [likewise] denotes ideal <foreign lang="ar">استعلآء</foreign> in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">لَهُمْ عَلَىَّ ذَنْبٌ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">A crime,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an offence, committed upon</hi> (or here, as in many other instances, it may be rendered <hi rend="ital">against</hi>) <hi rend="ital">me is imputable to them</hi>]: (Mughnee:) and so in the saying [in the Kur ii. 254 and xvii. 22], <foreign lang="ar">فَضَّلْنَا بَعْضَهُمْ عَلَى بَعْضٍ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">We have made some of them to have superiority over some</hi>]. (Es-Subkee, Mughnee, TA.) [See also <foreign lang="ar">أَنْتَ عَلَى عَيْنِى</foreign>, and and <foreign lang="ar">أَنْتَ عَلَى رَأْسِى</foreign>, voce <foreign lang="ar">عَيْنٌ</foreign>, first quarter.]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  It also denotes concomitance, like <foreign lang="ar">مَعَ</foreign>; as in the saying [in the Kur ii. 172], <foreign lang="ar">وَآتَى المَالَ عَلَى حُبِّهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And giveth property with</hi> (or <hi rend="ital">notwithstanding</hi>) <hi rend="ital">the love of it</hi>]; (Mughnee, K;) and so it is said to be used in the phrase, in a trad. respecting the alms of the breaking of the fast [of Ramadán], <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى كُلِّ حُرٍّ وَعَبْدٍ صَاعٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">With every free man and slave, a sáa</hi>], because the alms-gift of the breaking of the fast is not incumbent on the slave, but only on his master; (IAth, TA;) and so it is used in the [common] phrase, <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى أَنَّنِى رَاضٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">With</hi> (or <hi rend="ital">notwithstanding</hi>) <hi rend="ital">my being pleased,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">well pleased,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">content</hi>]. (Har p. 13.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  It also denotes transition, (Mughnee, K,) like <foreign lang="ar">عَنْ</foreign>; (Mughnee;) as in the saying (of El-Koheyf El- 'Okeylee, TA), <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">إِذَا رَضِيَتْ عَلَىَّ بَنُو قُشَيْرٍ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">لَعَمْرُ ٱللّٰهِ أَعْجَبَنِى رِضَاهَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">When the sons of Kusheyr shall be pleased,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">well pleased,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">content, with me,</hi> (or rather, if <foreign lang="ar">عَلَىَّ</foreign> here denote transition, <hi rend="ital">with what will proceed from me,</hi>) <hi rend="ital">by the everlasting existence of God, their being pleased,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">will induce in me admiration,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">pleasure</hi>], (Mughnee, K, * TA,) i. e. <foreign lang="ar">عَنِّى</foreign>; (Mughnee, TA;) or it may be that <foreign lang="ar">رَضِىَ</foreign> is made to imply the meaning of <foreign lang="ar">عَطَفَ</foreign> [which is trans. by means of <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى</foreign>]; (Mughnee;) or, as Ks says, it is made to accord with its contr. <foreign lang="ar">سَخِطَ</foreign>, (Mughnee, TA,) by its being made trans. by means of <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى</foreign>: (TA:) and so in the saying, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">فِى لَيْلَةٍ لَا نَرَى بِهَا أَحَدًا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">يَحْكِى عَلَيْنَا إِلَّا كَوَاكِبَهَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">In a nigh in which we shall not see any one that shall report what will proceed from us, except its stars</hi>], i. e., <foreign lang="ar">عَنَّا</foreign>; or it may be said that <foreign lang="ar">يَحْكِى</foreign> is [here] made to imply the meaning of <foreign lang="ar">يَنُِمُّ</foreign>. (Mughnee.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  It is also used to assign a cause, like <foreign lang="ar">ل</foreign>; as in the saying [in the Kur ii. 181], <foreign lang="ar">وَلِتُكَبِّرُوا ٱللّٰهَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى مَا هَدَاكُمْ</foreign>, (Mughnee, K,) meaning <foreign lang="ar">لِهِدَايَتِهِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">إِيَّاكُمْ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">And that ye should magnify God for,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">on account of, his rightly directing you</hi>]; (Mughnee;) [and in the same, vi. 90, &amp;c., <foreign lang="ar">لَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَسْأَلُكُمْ عَلَيْهِ أَجْرًا</foreign> i. e. <hi rend="ital">I will not ask of you for it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">on account of it, a recompense;</hi>] and as in the saying of Rabee'ah Ibn Makroom Ed-Dabbee, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">فَدَعَوْا نَزَالِ فَكُنْتُ أَوَّلَ نَازِلٍ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَعَلَامَ أَرْكَبُهُ إِذَا لَمْ أَنْزِلِ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> i. e. [<hi rend="ital">And they called out,</hi> “ <hi rend="ital">Alight;</hi> ” <hi rend="ital">and I was the first of any alighting:</hi>] <hi rend="ital">and for what</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">wherefore</hi>] <hi rend="ital">do I ride him if I do not alight</hi> when called upon to do so? (Ham p. 29. [<foreign lang="ar">عَلَامَ</foreign> is here, as usually, for <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى مَ</foreign>.])          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  It is also used in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">فِى</foreign> [generally followed by a noun significant of time]; (S, Mughnee, K; *) as in the saying [in the Kur xxviii. 14], <foreign lang="ar">وَدَخَلَ ٱلْمَدِينَةَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى حِينِ غَفْلَةٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And he entered the city in,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">during, a time of inadvertence</hi>]; (Mughnee, K;) and in the saying [in the same ii. 96], <foreign lang="ar">وَٱتَّبَعُوا مَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">تَتْلُو ٱلشَّيَاطِينُ عَلَى مُلْكِ سُلَيْمَانَ</foreign>, meaning, <foreign lang="ar">فِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">زَمَنِ مُلكِ سليمان</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">And they followed what the devils related,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">recited, in the time of,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">during, the reign of Suleymán</hi> (or <hi rend="ital">Solomon</hi>)]; (Mughnee;) and in the phrase, <foreign lang="ar">كَانَ كَذَا عَلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَهْدِ فُلَانٍ</foreign>, meaning, <foreign lang="ar">فِى عَهْدِهِ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">It was thus,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">such a thing was, in the time of such a one</hi>]: (S:) [and in like manner it is used in the saying in the Kur iii. 173, <foreign lang="ar">مَا كَانَ ٱللّٰهُ لِيَذَرَ ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى مَا أَنْتُمْ عَلَيْهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">God is not purposing to leave,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">certainly will not leave, the believers in that</hi> state <hi rend="ital">wherein ye are:</hi> and in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى سَفَرٍ</foreign>, in ii. 180 &amp;c. of the same, i. e. <hi rend="ital">In</hi> (or, as we also say, <hi rend="ital">on</hi>) <hi rend="ital">a journey:</hi> in like manner also] <foreign lang="ar">لَقَدْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">سَرَيْتُ عَلَى الظَّلَامِ</foreign>, in a verse of Aboo-Kebeer El-Hudhalee, means, <foreign lang="ar">فِى الظَّلَامِ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">I have journeyed by night in the darkness</hi>], <foreign lang="ar">فى الظلام</foreign> holding the place of a noun in the accus. case as a <foreign lang="ar">ظَرْف</foreign> [i. e. an adverbial noun of time or place]; or it may be in the place of a denotative of state, meaning <foreign lang="ar">وَأَنَا عَلَى الظَّلَامِ</foreign> i. e. <foreign lang="ar">رَاكِبٌ لَهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">riding upon the darkness</hi>]: (Ham p. 37:) and you say of one who was desiring to rise and hasten, <foreign lang="ar">رَأَيْتُهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى أَوْفَاضٍ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">I found him in a state of haste:</hi> see <foreign lang="ar">وَفْضٌ</foreign>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  [It also denotes conformity, accordance, adaptation, or agreement; as in the phrase, <foreign lang="ar">اِضْرِبْهُ عَلَى طَبْعِ هٰذَا</foreign> i. e. <hi rend="ital">Make thou it, fashion it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">mould it, conformably,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">according, to the model, make, fashion,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">mould, of this;</hi> (see <foreign lang="ar">طَبْعٌ</foreign>;) and in <foreign lang="ar">طُبِعَ عَلَى الشَّىْءِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">جُبِلَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">فُطِرَ</foreign> &amp;c. i. e. <hi rend="ital">He</hi> (a man) <hi rend="ital">was created conformably,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">with an adaptation</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a disposition, to the thing:</hi> (see 1 in art. <foreign lang="ar">طبع</foreign>:) so too in the phrase in the Kur xxiv. last verse, <foreign lang="ar">قَدْ يَعْلَمُ مَا أَنْتُمْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Certainly He knoweth that</hi> state of conduct and mind <hi rend="ital">to which ye are conforming yourselves;</hi> and in many other passages therein: thus also in the saying of Mohammad, <foreign lang="ar">كُلُّ مَوْلُودٍ يُولَدُ عَلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الفِطْرةِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Every infant is born in a state of conformity to the natural constitution with which he is created in his mother's womb in relation to the soul;</hi> (see art. <foreign lang="ar">فطر</foreign>;) and in the prov., mentioned by Meyd, <foreign lang="ar">النَّاسُ عَلَى دِينِ المُلُوكِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The people are in conformity to,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">are followers of,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">follow, the religion of the kings;</hi> and in the phrase, relating to a saying or an opinion, <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْهِ أَكْثَرُ العُلَمَآءِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Upon it most of the learned are in agreement;</hi> in which, as in other exs. of the same kind, a verb or a part. n., (in the last, for instance, <foreign lang="ar">مُجْمِعُونَ</foreign> or the like,) is understood.          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>  It also denotes a condition; as in the phrases, <foreign lang="ar">صَالَحَهُ عَلَى كَذَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He made peace,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">reconciliation,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a compromise, with him on the condition of such a thing,</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى أَنْ يَفْعَلَ كَذَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">on the condition of his doing such a thing.</hi>          <sense type="b" n="9">-b9-</sense>  And there are various other usages of this prep. depending upon verbs or part. ns. expressed or obviously understood in connection with them, too numerous to be here collected. Many of these will be found among the explanations of words with which they occur.]          <sense type="b" n="10">-b10-</sense>  It is also used in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ</foreign>; as in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">إِذَا ٱكْتَالُوا عَلَى ٱلنَّاسِ يَسْتَوْفُونَ</foreign>, (S, Mughnee, K,) in the Kur [lxxxiii. 2], meaning, <foreign lang="ar">مِنَ النَّاسِ</foreign> [i. e. Who, <hi rend="ital">when they take by measure from men, take fully</hi>], (S,) or, as in the T, <foreign lang="ar">عَنِ النَّاسِ</foreign> [which signifies the same]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="11">-b11-</sense>  It is also used in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">بِ</foreign>; (S, Mughnee, K;) as in the saying in the Kur [vii. 103], <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى أنْ لَا أَقُولَ عَلَى ٱللّٰهِ إِلَّا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ٱلْحَقَّ</foreign>, (Mughnee, K, *) meaning <foreign lang="ar">بِأَنْ</foreign>, (TA,) [i. e. <hi rend="ital">That I should not say of God</hi> aught <hi rend="ital">save the truth</hi>,] and Ubeí read with <foreign lang="ar">ب</foreign> [i. e. <foreign lang="ar">بِأَنْ</foreign>]; (Bd, Mughnee;) like as they say, <foreign lang="ar">رَمَيْتُ عَلَى القَوْسِ</foreign> [meaning <foreign lang="ar">بِالقَوْسِ</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">I shot with the bow</hi>], and <foreign lang="ar">جِئْتُ عَلَى حَالٍ حَسَنَةٍ</foreign> [meaning <foreign lang="ar">بِحَالٍ حَسَنَةٍ</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">I came in a good condition</hi>]; (Bd; [in which, and also voce <foreign lang="ar">حَقِيقٌ</foreign>, last sentence, see more;]) and they said also, <foreign lang="ar">اِرْكَبْ عَلَى ٱسْمِ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign> [meaning, <foreign lang="ar">بِسْمِ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">Mount thou in the name of God</hi>]: (Mughnee:) thus [too] it is used in the saying of Aboo-Dhu-eyb, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">يَسَرٌ يُفِيضُ عَلَى القِدَاحِ وَيَصْدَعُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [expl. in art. <foreign lang="ar">فيض</foreign>, conj. 4,] meaning <foreign lang="ar">بِالقِدَاحِ</foreign>: <pb n="2146"/> (S:) [and in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى يَدِهِ</foreign> i. e. <hi rend="ital">By his hand,</hi> or <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">by his means.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="12">-b12-</sense>  It is also used to denote an emendation, (Mughnee, K,) and a digression, or transition, (Mughnee,) like <foreign lang="ar">لٰكِنَّ</foreign>; (TA;) as in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ لَا يَدْخُلُ الجَنَّةَ لِسُوءِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">صَنِيعِهِ</foreign>, (Mughnee,) or <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ جَهَنَّمِىٌّ</foreign>, (K,) <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى أَنَّهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">لَا يّيْأَسُ مِنْ رَحْمةِ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign>, (Mughnee, K,) meaning <foreign lang="ar">لٰكِنَّهُ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">Such a one will not enter Paradise, because of the evilness of his deed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">conduct,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">such a one is hell-doomed; but,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">yet, he will not despair of the mercy of God</hi>]: (TA:) and thus it is used in the saying, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">بِكُلٍّ تَدَاوَيْنَا فَلَمْ يُشْفَ مَا بِنَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى أَنَّ قُرْبَ الدَّارِ خَيْرٌ مِنَ البُعْدِ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى أَنَّ قُرْبَ الدَّارِ لَيْسَ بِنَافِعٍ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">إِذَا كَانَ مَنْ تَهْوَاهُ لِيْسَ بِذِى وَدِّ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">With everything we treated,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">have treated, ourselves curatively, and what was in us was not,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">has not been, healed; but the nearness of the abode is better than the remoteness; but the nearness of the abode is not profitable when the person whom thou lovest is not endued with affection</hi>]: the poet invalidates by the first <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى</foreign> his saying <foreign lang="ar">فَلَمْ يُشْفَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مَا بِنَا</foreign>; and then, by the second <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى</foreign>, the clause immediately preceding it. (Mughnee.)          <sense type="b" n="13">-b13-</sense>  It is also redundant, for the purpose of compensation; as in the saying, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّ الكَرِيمَ وَأَبِيكَ يَعْتَمِلْ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">إِنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ يَوْمًا عَلَى مَنْ يَتَّكِلْ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> meaning <foreign lang="ar">مَنْ يَتَّكِلُ عَلَيْهِ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">Verily the generous, by thy father, will work for himself when he finds not, some day, him upon whom he may rely</hi>]; <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى</foreign> being added before <foreign lang="ar">مَنْ</foreign> for the purpose of compensation [for its omission in its proper place]: (Mughnee, K:) Es-Subkee says, it may be redundant, as in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَحْلِفُ عَلَى يَمِينٍ</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">لا احلف يَمِينًا</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">I will not swear an oath</hi>]. (TA.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  It is also a noun, having the meaning of <foreign lang="ar">فَوْق</foreign> [i. e. The <hi rend="ital">location that is above,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">over</hi>], this being the case when it is immediately followed by <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ</foreign>; (S, Msb, Mughnee, K; *) as in the saying (of Muzáhim-El-'Okeylee, describing a <foreign lang="ar">قَطَاة</foreign> [or sand-grouse, and, afterwards, its making a rumbling sound in its inside, from thirst], TA), <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">غَدَتْ مِنْ عَلَيْهِ بِعْدَ مَا تَمَّ ظِمْؤُهَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">It went away in the early morning from the location above it,</hi> (or, as we say, <hi rend="ital">from above it,</hi>) <hi rend="ital">after that her interval between two comings to water was complete</hi>]: (Msb, Mughnee, K: [and a similar ex. is cited in the S:]) or, accord. to As, meaning <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ عِنْدِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">from its vicinage</hi>]: and, used in this sense, as a noun, it admits before it no other prep. than <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ</foreign>. (Msb.)       <sense type="A" n="3">-A3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْكَ</foreign> is also a verbal noun, used as an incentive: (TA:) you say, <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْكَ زَيْدًا</foreign>, (S, K, TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">بِزَيْدٍ</foreign>, (TA,) meaning <hi rend="ital">Take thou Zeyd;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">take thou hold of Zeyd:</hi> (S, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">keep thou,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">cleave thou, to Zeyd:</hi> (K, TA:) and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْكَ بِكَذَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">keep thou to such a thing:</hi> (El-Munáwee, TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">ب</foreign>:) [thus] it is said in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْكَ باِلرِّفْقِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Keep thou to gentleness</hi>]. (El-Jámi' es-Sagheer.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  And [in like manner] you say, <foreign lang="ar">عَلَىَّ زَيْدًا</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">بِزَيْدٍ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Give thou me,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">present thou to me, Zeyd:</hi> (S, TA:) [or, more commonly, <hi rend="ital">bring thou to me Zeyd:</hi>] you say, <foreign lang="ar">عَلَىَّ بِكَذَا</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">bring thou to me such a thing.</hi> (MA.)    </entryFree>26:T4041,<entryFree id="n30391" key="عَلَا" type="main">

      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30391-1" target="تعلّى" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n30395"/></foreign> [which last see also below]; (K;) <hi rend="ital">It</hi> (a thing, Msb) <hi rend="ital">was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, high, elevated,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">lofty;</hi> (Msb, K; *) syn. <foreign lang="ar">اِرْتَفَعَ</foreign>; (Msb;) and so   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30391-2" target="تعالى" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n30396"/></foreign>: (S, K:) or you say, <foreign lang="ar">عَلَا فِى المَكَانِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">it was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, high,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">elevated, in place</hi>], aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَعْلُو</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عُلُوٌّ</foreign>: (S:) and <foreign lang="ar">عَلِىَ فِى الشَّرَفِ</foreign> [<assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">he was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, high,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">elevated,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">exalted, in dignity,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">nobility</hi>], (S, Mgh,) with kesr, (S,) aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَعْلَى</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عَلَآءٌ</foreign>; (S, Mgh;) and also <foreign lang="ar">عَلَا</foreign>, with fet-h, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَعْلَى</foreign>: a poet says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">لَمَّا عَلَا كَعْبُكَ لِى عَلِيتُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">When thy nobility became exalted to me, I became exalted</hi>]; thus combining the two dial. vars.: (S:) or you say, <foreign lang="ar">عَلِىَ فِى المَكَارِمِ</foreign> [<assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">he was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, eminent in generous,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">honourable, actions</hi> or <hi rend="ital">qualities</hi>], inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عَلَآءٌ</foreign> [in some copies of the K <foreign lang="ar">عَلًا</foreign>]; (Msb, K;) and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَا</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عُلُوٌّ</foreign>; (K;) and thus the two verbs are used in the saying of the poet cited above: (TA:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30391-3" target="استعلى" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, said of a man, signifies the same as <foreign lang="ar">عَلَا</foreign>. (S.) [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">عَلَتِ الشَّمْسُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The sun became high;</hi> as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30391-4" target="اِعْتَلَت" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>: (Nawádir el-Aaráb, TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">دلك</foreign>:) and [hence,] <foreign lang="ar">عَلَا النَّهَارُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The day became advanced, the sun being somewhat high;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">اِرْتَفَعَ</foreign> [q. v.]; as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30391-5" target="اعتلى" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30391-6" target="استعلى" n="6" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>. (K.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَا فِى المَكَانِ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عُلُوٌّ</foreign>, signifies [also] <hi rend="ital">He ascended the place,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">upon the place;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">صَعِدَ</foreign>: and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَوْتُ عَلَى الجَبَلِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَوْتُ أَعْلَاهُ</foreign> are syn. [as meaning <hi rend="ital">I ascended the mountain,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">upon the mountain,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">upon the top,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">highest part, thereof</hi>]: and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَوْتُهُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَوْتُ فِيهِ</foreign> signify <hi rend="ital">I ascended it;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">رَقِيتُ</foreign>
